<ul>
<li><sup>1</sup> When the #14 of <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Robert" title="René Robert">Robert</a> and the #7 of <a href="/wiki/Rick_Martin" title="Rick Martin">Martin</a> were retired, <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Perreault" title="Gilbert Perreault">Gilbert Perreault</a> was present, as the entire "<a href="/wiki/The_French_Connection_(ice_hockey)" title="The French Connection (ice hockey)">French Connection</a>" line was given retirement together. Perreault's #11 was lowered and then raised back in the center under the French Connection banner, as shown above.</li>
<li><b>SHK III and NRK</b> (team founders <a href="/wiki/Seymour_H._Knox_III" title="Seymour H. Knox III">Seymour H. Knox III</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northrup_R._Knox" title="Northrup R. Knox">Northrup R. Knox</a>. Two banners bearing their initials and the Sabres blue and gold reside in the First Niagara Center's rafters.)</li>
<li>The number 00 was not allowed on any NHL team, since <a href="/wiki/Martin_Biron" title="Martin Biron">Martin Biron</a> was the last player to wear that sweater number.</li>
<li>Although number 89 is not officially retired by the team, it has not been reissued since the departure of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Mogilny" title="Alexander Mogilny">Alexander Mogilny</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cory_Conacher" title="Cory Conacher">Cory Conacher</a> switched to 88 expressly out of deference to Mogilny.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> Likewise, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Miller" title="Ryan Miller">Ryan Miller</a>, who traditionally wears 39, wore 30 during his time with the Sabres out of deference to Hasek, long before 39 was announced to be retired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="NHL_awards_and_trophies">NHL awards and trophies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Buffalo_Sabres&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: NHL awards and trophies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Front_Office">Front Office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Buffalo_Sabres&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Front Office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Buffalo_Sabres_general_managers" title="List of Buffalo Sabres general managers">List of Buffalo Sabres general managers</a>.</div>
<p>The current general manager of the Sabres is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tim_Murray_(ice_hockey,_born_1963)" title="Tim Murray (ice hockey, born 1963)">Tim Murray</a>, who was hired January 9, 2014. <a href="/wiki/Craig_Patrick" title="Craig Patrick">Craig Patrick</a> serves as a special advisor to the team. <a href="/wiki/Russ_Brandon" title="Russ Brandon">Russ Brandon</a> serves as team president.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Head_coaches">Head coaches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Buffalo_Sabres&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Head coaches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Buffalo_Sabres_head_coaches" title="List of Buffalo Sabres head coaches">List of Buffalo Sabres head coaches</a>.</div>
<p>The head coach position is currently held by <a href="/wiki/Dan_Bylsma" title="Dan Bylsma">Dan Bylsma</a>, who was hired May 28, 2015. Tom Ward, <a href="/wiki/Terry_Murray" title="Terry Murray">Terry Murray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adam_Mair" title="Adam Mair">Adam Mair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Krys_Barch" title="Krys Barch">Krys Barch</a> serve as assistants;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Allen_(ice_hockey)" title="Andrew Allen (ice hockey)">Andrew Allen</a> serves as goaltending coach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Of the 17 head coaches the Sabres have used in their history, six of them had previously played for the Sabres during their playing career: <a href="/wiki/Floyd_Smith" title="Floyd Smith">Floyd Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Inglis_(ice_hockey)" title="Bill Inglis (ice hockey)">Bill Inglis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Schoenfeld" title="Jim Schoenfeld">Jim Schoenfeld</a>, <a href="/wiki/Craig_Ramsay" title="Craig Ramsay">Craig Ramsay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Dudley" title="Rick Dudley">Rick Dudley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lindy_Ruff" title="Lindy Ruff">Lindy Ruff</a>. Two others, Bylsma and <a href="/wiki/Ted_Nolan" title="Ted Nolan">Ted Nolan</a>, had played in the Sabres' farm system.</p>

<dl>
<dt>Notes</dt>

<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: upper-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-a-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-a_4-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The name was selected because, as public relations director Chuck Barr wrote in a press release, 'a sabre is renowned as a clean, sharp, decisive and penetrating weapon on offense, as well as a strong parrying weapon on defense.'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-b-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-b_5-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The word <i>sabre</i> is rarely spelled as such in the United States (where it is <i>saber</i>) but, as with many words which can end either in <b>-re</b> or <b>-er</b>, it is spelled <i>sabre</i> in neighbouring Canada.</span></li>
</ol>
